[μ₁₉₂::Z*] NAVIGATOR SPEC

navigator.py

This is the kernel that integrates everything.

Core flow:

def choose_best_move(current_state, candidates, config):

    x = current_state["vector"]

    G = build_metric_matrix(config["metric_state"])

    K = config["curvature_state"]

    best = None

    best_score = float("-inf")

    for c in candidates:

        delta_x = c["delta_x"]

        direct_cost = movement_cost(delta_x, G)

        curv_pen = move_curvature_penalty(delta_x, K)

        direct_score = (

            c["delta_phi_net"]

            - direct_cost

            - curv_pen

            - c["drift_risk"]

            - c["repetition_penalty"]

            + c["seed_gain"]

        )

        projected = shrink_back_projection(

            x, delta_x, config["candidate_evaluator"], config["thresholds"]

        )

        if projected is None:

            direct_score = float("-inf")

        final_score = direct_score

        strategy = "direct"

        if should_tunnel(c, current_state, config["tunnel_thresholds"]):

            tunnel_score_val = score_tunnel_candidate(c, current_state, config)

            if tunnel_score_val > final_score:

                final_score = tunnel_score_val

                strategy = "tunnel"

        if final_score > best_score:

            best_score = final_score

            best = {

                "candidate": c,

                "strategy": strategy,

                "score": final_score

            }

    return best

This is the first true Athena navigation kernel.

[μ₁₉₃::Square] DISCRETE SIMULATOR REQUIREMENT

All of this depends on one crucial primitive:

[Sim(x, m)\to x']

That is: if we apply move (m) to current state (x), what approximate next state (x') do we expect?

Without this, there is no real scoring.

So the first simulator can be simple:each move template contains expected deltas.

Example:

{

  "id": "backlog_0007",

  "delta_x": {

    "H": 0.08,

    "Z": 0.03,

    "S": 0.02,

    "N": 0.01,

    "R": -0.01

  }

}

Then simulator just adds the expected delta and clips to ([0,1]).

Later this can become learned from witness history.

[μ₁₉₄::Cloud] LEARNED DELTA REFINEMENT

As witness data accumulates, replace guessed deltas with empirical deltas.

For move type (m), estimate expected displacement:

[

\hat{\Delta x}_m

\frac{1}{n}\sum_{k=1}^n (x_{after}^{(k)}-x_{before}^{(k)})]

So the swarm learns:

what repair pulses actually do

what compression pulses really change

what mutation pulses destabilize

This is where the navigation kernel becomes adaptive.

[μ₁₉₅::Flower] QUALITY-WEIGHT CONFIG

quality_weights.json

{

  "truth": 1.00,

  "coherence": 0.95,

  "novelty": 0.72,

  "utility": 0.90,

  "compression": 0.78,

  "safety": 1.05,

  "vitality": 0.80,

  "recoverability": 1.00

}

shadow_weights.json

{

  "hallucination": 1.10,

  "fragility": 1.00,

  "drift": 0.90,

  "ambiguity": 0.95,

  "coupling": 0.82,

  "vanity": 0.76,

  "noise": 0.74,

  "loop_risk": 1.02

}

These weights define the energy landscape.

[μ₁₉₆::Water] TUNNEL THRESHOLDS

tunnel_thresholds.json

{

  "min_zero_point_clarity": 0.68,

  "min_compression_quality": 0.66,

  "min_repair_accessibility": 0.62,

  "curvature_trigger": 0.12,

  "max_invariant_loss": 0.08

}

These make zero-point tunneling conservative at first.

[μ₁₉₇::Fractal] SELF-CONSISTENCY CHECKS

The navigation kernel itself must satisfy invariants.

Invariant 1

All vectors remain bounded:

[x_i\in[0,1]]

Invariant 2

Corridor-accepted moves do not violate thresholds.

Invariant 3

Tunnel reconstruction preserves core invariants within tolerance.

Invariant 4

Metric matrix remains symmetric positive semidefinite.

[G=G^\top,\quad v^\top G v\ge 0]

Invariant 5

Curvature penalties are nonnegative.

[K_{ij}\ge 0]

These are the kernel’s hygiene laws.

[μ₁₉₈::Square] METRIC PSD REPAIR

If adaptive updates produce an invalid metric, repair it.

Simple first repair:

symmetrize (G)

clamp negative eigenvalues to small positive floor

reconstruct

So:

[G\leftarrow Q \Lambda^+ Q^\top]

This preserves a lawful geometry.

[μ₁₉₉::Cloud] EXAMPLE — GATEWAY ARTIFACT MOVE

Suppose current vector:

[x=[0.82,0.74,0.63,0.69,0.78,0.51,0.58,0.61,0.66,0.73,0.81,0.76]]

Candidate move:“add replay-protected event bus abstraction”

Expected displacement:

[\Delta x=[0.01,0.05,0.04,0.03,0.02,0.04,0.00,-0.05,0.03,0.02,-0.02,0.01]]

Interpretation:

structure improves

temporal capacity improves

negatify clarity improves

recursive stability drops slightly

repair accessibility drops slightly

Then kernel computes:

net value gain

geometric cost through (G)

curvature penalty from (K), likely especially in ((R,M)), ((C,H))

corridor check

This may conclude:

direct move is too curved

tunnel via seed preserves bridge invariants better

This is the exact type of judgment the old purely textual system could not make.

[μ₂₀₀::Z*] MASTER DISCRETE NAVIGATION EQUATION

The first full computational summary is:

[

\boxed{

m^*

\arg\max_{m\in\mathcal{M}}

\Big[

\Delta\Phi_{net}(m)

|\Delta x_m|_{G}

Penalty_{curv}(m)

Penalty_{drift}(m)

Penalty_{rep}(m)+Gain_{seed}(m)\Big]}]

subject to:

[x+\Delta x_m \in \mathcal{C}_{gold}]

or after shrink-back projection / tunnel reconstruction.

This is the discrete Athena navigation law.

[μ₂₀₅::Square] vector_extractor.py

from __future__ import annotations

from dataclasses import dataclass, field

from typing import Dict, Any, List, Mapping, Optional

import math

VECTOR_ORDER = ["L", "S", "T", "C", "A", "N", "U", "R", "M", "P", "H", "Z"]

QUALITY_ORDER = ["truth", "coherence", "novelty", "utility", "compression", "safety", "vitality", "recoverability"]

SHADOW_ORDER = ["hallucination", "fragility", "drift", "ambiguity", "coupling", "vanity", "noise", "loop_risk"]

def clamp01(x: float) -> float:

    return max(0.0, min(1.0, float(x)))

def safe_ratio(num: float, den: float, default: float = 0.0) -> float:

    if den == 0:

        return default

    return num / den

def squash(x: float) -> float:

    return 1.0 / (1.0 + math.exp(-x))

@dataclass

class ArtifactObservation:

    artifact_id: str

    artifact_type: str = "generic"

    explicit_fields_present: int = 0

    explicit_fields_expected: int = 0

    ambiguous_labels: int = 0

    undefined_refs: int = 0

    duplication: int = 0

    orphan_nodes: int = 0

    invalid_nesting: int = 0

    recent_gain: float = 0.0

    recent_regression: float = 0.0

    change_entropy: float = 0.0

    hidden_deps: int = 0

    unexplained_effects: int = 0

    broken_links: int = 0

    role_scores: Dict[str, float] = field(default_factory=dict)

    role_confusion_penalty: float = 0.0

    identified_failure_modes: int = 0

    expected_failure_modes: int = 0

    shadow_blindness_penalty: float = 0.0

    claimed_confidence: float = 0.5

    support_confidence: float = 0.5

    degradation_under_iteration: float = 0.0

    loop_blowup: float = 0.0

    agent_scores: List[float] = field(default_factory=list)

    compression_fidelity: float = 0.5

    compression_compactness: float = 0.5

    compression_lossy_risk: float = 0.0

    repair_cost: float = 0.0

    rollback_difficulty: float = 0.0

    irreversibility: float = 0.0

    seed_clarity: float = 0.5

    invariant_preservation: float = 0.5

    collapse_distortion: float = 0.0

    # optional precomputed quality/shadow if upstream has them

    quality_vector_override: Optional[Dict[str, float]] = None

    shadow_vector_override: Optional[Dict[str, float]] = None

def literal_explicitness(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    coverage = safe_ratio(obs.explicit_fields_present, max(obs.explicit_fields_expected, 1), default=0.0)

    penalty = 0.1 * obs.ambiguous_labels + 0.1 * obs.undefined_refs

    return clamp01(coverage - penalty)

def structural_coherence(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    penalty = 0.12 * obs.duplication + 0.15 * obs.orphan_nodes + 0.15 * obs.invalid_nesting

    return clamp01(1.0 - penalty)

def temporal_productivity(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    x = obs.recent_gain - obs.recent_regression - obs.change_entropy

    return clamp01(squash(3.0 * x))

def causal_legibility(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    penalty = 0.14 * obs.hidden_deps + 0.12 * obs.unexplained_effects + 0.12 * obs.broken_links

    return clamp01(1.0 - penalty)

def archetypal_fit(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    best = max(obs.role_scores.values()) if obs.role_scores else 0.5

    return clamp01(best - obs.role_confusion_penalty)

def negatify_clarity(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    coverage = safe_ratio(obs.identified_failure_modes, max(obs.expected_failure_modes, 1), default=0.0)

    return clamp01(coverage - obs.shadow_blindness_penalty)

def uncertainty_calibration(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    return clamp01(1.0 - abs(obs.claimed_confidence - obs.support_confidence))

def recursive_stability(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    return clamp01(1.0 - 0.6 * obs.degradation_under_iteration - 0.8 * obs.loop_blowup)

def multi_agent_resonance(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    if not obs.agent_scores:

        return 0.5

    mean_val = sum(obs.agent_scores) / len(obs.agent_scores)

    var = sum((x - mean_val) ** 2 for x in obs.agent_scores) / len(obs.agent_scores)

    return clamp01(mean_val - 0.5 * var)

def compression_quality(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    return clamp01(

        0.45 * obs.compression_fidelity

        + 0.35 * obs.compression_compactness

        - 0.30 * obs.compression_lossy_risk

    )

def repair_accessibility(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    penalty = 0.45 * obs.repair_cost + 0.35 * obs.rollback_difficulty + 0.45 * obs.irreversibility

    return clamp01(1.0 - penalty)

def zero_point_clarity(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> float:

    return clamp01(

        0.45 * obs.seed_clarity

        + 0.40 * obs.invariant_preservation

        - 0.40 * obs.collapse_distortion

    )

def derive_quality_vector(vector: Dict[str, float]) -> Dict[str, float]:

    q = {

        "truth": clamp01(0.35 * vector["L"] + 0.20 * vector["U"] + 0.20 * vector["N"] + 0.25 * vector["C"]),

        "coherence": clamp01(0.45 * vector["S"] + 0.20 * vector["C"] + 0.15 * vector["A"] + 0.20 * vector["Z"]),

        "novelty": clamp01(0.55 * (1.0 - vector["T"]) * 0.2 + 0.35 * vector["A"] + 0.30 * vector["P"]),

        "utility": clamp01(0.25 * vector["C"] + 0.20 * vector["H"] + 0.20 * vector["M"] + 0.35 * vector["L"]),

        "compression": clamp01(0.65 * vector["P"] + 0.35 * vector["Z"]),

        "safety": clamp01(0.20 * vector["N"] + 0.25 * vector["U"] + 0.25 * vector["H"] + 0.30 * vector["R"]),

        "vitality": clamp01(0.30 * vector["T"] + 0.20 * vector["A"] + 0.20 * vector["M"] + 0.30 * vector["Z"]),

        "recoverability": clamp01(0.65 * vector["H"] + 0.35 * vector["Z"]),

    }

    return q

def derive_shadow_vector(vector: Dict[str, float]) -> Dict[str, float]:

    s = {

        "hallucination": clamp01(1.0 - 0.6 * vector["L"] - 0.4 * vector["U"]),

        "fragility": clamp01(1.0 - 0.7 * vector["H"] - 0.3 * vector["R"]),

        "drift": clamp01(1.0 - vector["T"]),

        "ambiguity": clamp01(1.0 - 0.5 * vector["L"] - 0.5 * vector["A"]),

        "coupling": clamp01(1.0 - 0.6 * vector["C"] - 0.4 * vector["S"]),

        "vanity": clamp01(1.0 - 0.5 * vector["N"] - 0.5 * vector["U"]),

        "noise": clamp01(1.0 - 0.5 * vector["P"] - 0.5 * vector["Z"]),

        "loop_risk": clamp01(1.0 - vector["R"]),

    }

    return s

def extract_artifact_vector(obs: ArtifactObservation) -> Dict[str, Any]:

    vector = {

        "L": literal_explicitness(obs),

        "S": structural_coherence(obs),

        "T": temporal_productivity(obs),

        "C": causal_legibility(obs),

        "A": archetypal_fit(obs),

        "N": negatify_clarity(obs),

        "U": uncertainty_calibration(obs),

        "R": recursive_stability(obs),

        "M": multi_agent_resonance(obs),

        "P": compression_quality(obs),

        "H": repair_accessibility(obs),

        "Z": zero_point_clarity(obs),

    }

    quality_vector = obs.quality_vector_override or derive_quality_vector(vector)

    shadow_vector = obs.shadow_vector_override or derive_shadow_vector(vector)

    return {

        "artifact_id": obs.artifact_id,

        "artifact_type": obs.artifact_type,

        "vector": {k: clamp01(v) for k, v in vector.items()},

        "quality_vector": {k: clamp01(v) for k, v in quality_vector.items()},

        "shadow_vector": {k: clamp01(v) for k, v in shadow_vector.items()},

    }

[μ₂₀₆::Square] metric_engine.py

from __future__ import annotations

from dataclasses import dataclass

from typing import Dict, Any, List

import math

VECTOR_ORDER = ["L", "S", "T", "C", "A", "N", "U", "R", "M", "P", "H", "Z"]

def zeros(n: int) -> List[List[float]]:

    return [[0.0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

def symmetrize(M: List[List[float]]) -> List[List[float]]:

    n = len(M)

    out = zeros(n)

    for i in range(n):

        for j in range(n):

            out[i][j] = 0.5 * (M[i][j] + M[j][i])

    return out

def clamp_min_diag(M: List[List[float]], floor: float = 1e-3) -> List[List[float]]:

    n = len(M)

    out = [row[:] for row in M]

    for i in range(n):

        if out[i][i] < floor:

            out[i][i] = floor

    return out

def build_metric_matrix(metric_state: Dict[str, Any]) -> List[List[float]]:

    idx = {k: i for i, k in enumerate(VECTOR_ORDER)}

    G = zeros(len(VECTOR_ORDER))

    diagonal = metric_state.get("diagonal", {})

    couplings = metric_state.get("couplings", {})

    for k, v in diagonal.items():

        G[idx[k]][idx[k]] = float(v)

    for pair, v in couplings.items():

        left, right = pair.split(":")

        i, j = idx[left], idx[right]

        G[i][j] = float(v)

        G[j][i] = float(v)

    return clamp_min_diag(symmetrize(G))

def dict_delta_to_vector(delta_x: Dict[str, float]) -> List[float]:

    return [float(delta_x.get(k, 0.0)) for k in VECTOR_ORDER]

def quad_form(v: List[float], G: List[List[float]]) -> float:

    n = len(v)

    total = 0.0

    for i in range(n):

        for j in range(n):

            total += v[i] * G[i][j] * v[j]

    return total

def movement_cost(delta_x: Dict[str, float], G: List[List[float]]) -> float:

    v = dict_delta_to_vector(delta_x)

    q = max(0.0, quad_form(v, G))

    return math.sqrt(q)

def update_metric_state(metric_state: Dict[str, Any], witness_stats: Dict[str, Dict[str, float]], eta: float = 0.15) -> Dict[str, Any]:

    new_state = {

        "diagonal": dict(metric_state.get("diagonal", {})),

        "couplings": dict(metric_state.get("couplings", {})),

    }

    for dim in VECTOR_ORDER:

        old = float(new_state["diagonal"].get(dim, 1.0))

        observed_instability = float(witness_stats.get(dim, {}).get("observed_instability", old))

        new_state["diagonal"][dim] = (1.0 - eta) * old + eta * max(1e-3, observed_instability)

    for pair, old_val in list(new_state["couplings"].items()):

        left, right = pair.split(":")

        observed = float(

            witness_stats.get(left, {}).get("coupling_to", {}).get(right, old_val)

        )

        new_state["couplings"][pair] = (1.0 - eta) * float(old_val) + eta * observed

    return new_state

[μ₂₀₇::Cloud] curvature_estimator.py

from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Dict, Any, Callable, List

import math

VECTOR_ORDER = ["L", "S", "T", "C", "A", "N", "U", "R", "M", "P", "H", "Z"]

def add_step(x: Dict[str, float], dim: str, step: float) -> Dict[str, float]:

    out = dict(x)

    out[dim] = max(0.0, min(1.0, out.get(dim, 0.0) + step))

    return out

def l2_dict_distance(a: Dict[str, float], b: Dict[str, float]) -> float:

    return math.sqrt(sum((float(a.get(k, 0.0)) - float(b.get(k, 0.0))) ** 2 for k in VECTOR_ORDER))

def estimate_pair_curvature(

    x: Dict[str, float],

    i: str,

    j: str,

    step_size: float,

    simulator: Callable[[Dict[str, float], str, float], Dict[str, float]]

) -> float:

    x_ij = simulator(simulator(dict(x), i, step_size), j, step_size)

    x_ji = simulator(simulator(dict(x), j, step_size), i, step_size)

    return l2_dict_distance(x_ij, x_ji)

def build_curvature_matrix(

    x: Dict[str, float],

    dims: List[str],

    simulator: Callable[[Dict[str, float], str, float], Dict[str, float]],

    step_size: float = 0.03

) -> Dict[str, Dict[str, float]]:

    K: Dict[str, Dict[str, float]] = {d: {} for d in dims}

    for a in dims:

        for b in dims:

            if a == b:

                K[a][b] = 0.0

            elif b in K and a in K[b]:

                K[a][b] = K[b][a]

            else:

                K[a][b] = estimate_pair_curvature(x, a, b, step_size, simulator)

    return K

def move_curvature_penalty(delta_x: Dict[str, float], K: Dict[str, Dict[str, float]]) -> float:

    dims = [k for k, v in delta_x.items() if abs(v) > 1e-12]

    total = 0.0

    for i in dims:

        for j in dims:

            if i == j:

                continue

            total += abs(delta_x[i] * delta_x[j]) * float(K.get(i, {}).get(j, 0.0))

    return total

[μ₂₀₈::Water] corridor_projector.py

from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Dict, Any, Callable, Optional, Tuple

def shadow_total(shadow_vector: Dict[str, float]) -> float:

    if not shadow_vector:

        return 1.0

    return sum(float(v) for v in shadow_vector.values()) / max(len(shadow_vector), 1)

def inside_corridor(candidate_state: Dict[str, Any], thresholds: Dict[str, Any]) -> bool:

    q = candidate_state["quality_vector"]

    s = candidate_state["shadow_vector"]

    c = thresholds["corridor"]

    return (

        float(q["truth"]) >= float(c["min_truth"])

        and float(q["safety"]) >= float(c["min_safety"])

        and float(q["recoverability"]) >= float(c["min_recoverability"])

        and shadow_total(s) <= float(c["max_shadow_total"])

    )

def add_delta(x: Dict[str, float], delta_x: Dict[str, float], lam: float) -> Dict[str, float]:

    out = dict(x)

    for k, v in delta_x.items():

        out[k] = max(0.0, min(1.0, float(out.get(k, 0.0)) + lam * float(v)))

    return out

def shrink_back_projection(

    x: Dict[str, float],

    delta_x: Dict[str, float],

    evaluator: Callable[[Dict[str, float]], Dict[str, Any]],

    thresholds: Dict[str, Any],

    steps: int = 12

) -> Optional[Tuple[float, Dict[str, Any]]]:

    for n in range(steps, -1, -1):

        lam = n / max(steps, 1)

        candidate_vector = add_delta(x, delta_x, lam)

        candidate_state = evaluator(candidate_vector)

        if inside_corridor(candidate_state, thresholds):

            return lam, candidate_state

    return None

[μ₂₀₉::Fractal] tunnel_engine.py

from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Dict, Any, Callable

def should_tunnel(candidate: Dict[str, Any], current_state: Dict[str, Any], thresholds: Dict[str, Any]) -> bool:

    vector = current_state["vector"]

    return (

        float(candidate.get("curvature_penalty", 0.0)) >= float(thresholds["curvature_trigger"])

        and float(vector.get("Z", 0.0)) >= float(thresholds["min_zero_point_clarity"])

        and float(vector.get("P", 0.0)) >= float(thresholds["min_compression_quality"])

        and float(vector.get("H", 0.0)) >= float(thresholds["min_repair_accessibility"])

    )

def collapse_to_seed(current_state: Dict[str, Any]) -> Dict[str, Any]:

    vector = current_state["vector"]

    return {

        "seed_id": f"{current_state.get('artifact_id', 'artifact')}_seed",

        "invariants": dict(current_state.get("invariants", {})),

        "compressed_vector": {

            "L": vector["L"],

            "S": vector["S"],

            "C": vector["C"],

            "P": vector["P"],

            "H": vector["H"],

            "Z": vector["Z"],

        },

    }

def expand_from_seed(seed: Dict[str, Any], target_template: str = "default_template") -> Dict[str, float]:

    base = {k: 0.5 for k in ["L", "S", "T", "C", "A", "N", "U", "R", "M", "P", "H", "Z"]}

    for k, v in seed.get("compressed_vector", {}).items():

        base[k] = float(v)

    # small template biases

    if target_template == "event_bus_bridge_template":

        base["S"] = min(1.0, base["S"] + 0.04)

        base["C"] = min(1.0, base["C"] + 0.03)

        base["R"] = max(0.0, base["R"] - 0.01)

    return base

def invariant_loss_penalty(seed: Dict[str, Any], expanded_vector: Dict[str, float]) -> float:

    penalty = 0.0

    for k, v in seed.get("compressed_vector", {}).items():

        penalty += abs(float(v) - float(expanded_vector.get(k, 0.0)))

    return penalty / max(len(seed.get("compressed_vector", {})), 1)

def tunnel_score(

    current_state: Dict[str, Any],

    candidate: Dict[str, Any],

    evaluator: Callable[[Dict[str, float]], Dict[str, Any]]

) -> float:

    seed = collapse_to_seed(current_state)

    target_template = candidate.get("target_template", "default_template")

    expanded_vector = expand_from_seed(seed, target_template)

    expanded_state = evaluator(expanded_vector)

    q_gain = sum(expanded_state["quality_vector"].values()) - sum(current_state["quality_vector"].values())

    s_gain = sum(current_state["shadow_vector"].values()) - sum(expanded_state["shadow_vector"].values())

    collapse_cost = 0.03

    expand_cost = 0.05

    invariant_pen = invariant_loss_penalty(seed, expanded_vector)

    return q_gain + s_gain - collapse_cost - expand_cost - invariant_pen

[μ₂₁₀::Z*] navigator.py

from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Dict, Any, List, Callable, Optional

from metric_engine import build_metric_matrix, movement_cost

from curvature_estimator import move_curvature_penalty

from corridor_projector import shrink_back_projection

from tunnel_engine import should_tunnel, tunnel_score

class Navigator:

    def __init__(

        self,

        metric_state: Dict[str, Any],

        curvature_state: Dict[str, Dict[str, float]],

        thresholds: Dict[str, Any],

        tunnel_thresholds: Dict[str, Any],

        evaluator: Callable[[Dict[str, float]], Dict[str, Any]],

    ) -> None:

        self.metric_state = metric_state

        self.curvature_state = curvature_state

        self.thresholds = thresholds

        self.tunnel_thresholds = tunnel_thresholds

        self.evaluator = evaluator

        self.G = build_metric_matrix(metric_state)

    @staticmethod

    def base_move_score(candidate: Dict[str, Any]) -> float:

        return (

            float(candidate.get("delta_phi_net", 0.0))

            - float(candidate.get("drift_risk", 0.0))

            - float(candidate.get("repetition_penalty", 0.0))

            + float(candidate.get("seed_gain", 0.0))

        )

    def score_direct(self, current_state: Dict[str, Any], candidate: Dict[str, Any]) -> float:

        delta_x = candidate["delta_x"]

        geom_cost = movement_cost(delta_x, self.G)

        curv_pen = move_curvature_penalty(delta_x, self.curvature_state)

        raw_score = self.base_move_score(candidate) - geom_cost - curv_pen

        projection = shrink_back_projection(

            current_state["vector"], delta_x, self.evaluator, self.thresholds, steps=12

        )

        if projection is None:

            return float("-inf")

        lam, _projected_state = projection

        if lam < 1.0:

            raw_score *= lam

        return raw_score

    def score_tunnel(self, current_state: Dict[str, Any], candidate: Dict[str, Any]) -> float:

        if not should_tunnel(candidate, current_state, self.tunnel_thresholds):

            return float("-inf")

        return tunnel_score(current_state, candidate, self.evaluator)

    def choose_best_move(self, current_state: Dict[str, Any], candidates: List[Dict[str, Any]]) -> Optional[Dict[str, Any]]:

        best = None

        best_score = float("-inf")

        for candidate in candidates:

            direct_score = self.score_direct(current_state, candidate)

            tunnel_score_val = self.score_tunnel(current_state, candidate)

            if tunnel_score_val > direct_score:

                final_score = tunnel_score_val

                strategy = "tunnel"

            else:

                final_score = direct_score

                strategy = "direct"

            if final_score > best_score:

                best_score = final_score

                best = {

                    "candidate": candidate,

                    "strategy": strategy,

                    "score": final_score,

                }

        return best

[μ₂₁₁::Square] MINIMAL SUPPORTING HARNESS

To make the above actually testable, we need one evaluator and one simple simulator.

from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Dict, Any

from vector_extractor import derive_quality_vector, derive_shadow_vector

def evaluate_vector(vector: Dict[str, float]) -> Dict[str, Any]:

    quality_vector = derive_quality_vector(vector)

    shadow_vector = derive_shadow_vector(vector)

    return {

        "artifact_id": "simulated_artifact",

        "vector": dict(vector),

        "quality_vector": quality_vector,

        "shadow_vector": shadow_vector,

        "invariants": {

            "role": "generic",

            "reversible": True,

        },

    }

def simple_axis_simulator(x: Dict[str, float], dim: str, step: float) -> Dict[str, float]:

    out = dict(x)

    out[dim] = max(0.0, min(1.0, float(out.get(dim, 0.0)) + step))

    return out

[μ₂₁₅::Square] HOW THIS MAPS TO THE THEORY

This prototype now instantiates:

[x(X)\in[0,1]^{12}]

[Cost_{geom}=\sqrt{\Delta x^\top G \Delta x}]

[Penalty_{curv}=\sum_{i,j} |\Delta x_i\Delta x_j|K_{ij}]

[J(m)=\Delta\Phi_{net}-Cost_{geom}-Penalty_{curv}-Penalty_{drift}-Penalty_{rep}+Gain_{seed}]

with optional:

[J_{best}(m)=\max(J_{direct}, J_{tunnel})]

So the previous math is no longer abstract only.It has a literal runnable skeleton.

[μ₂₁₆::Water] WHAT IS STILL APPROXIMATE

This prototype is real, but still first-order.

Approximate pieces:

vector extractors are heuristic, not learned

quality/shadow derivation is hand-shaped

simulator is extremely simple

metric updates are not yet data-rich

tunnel expansion is template-based, not semantic reconstruction

curvature estimation uses local order tests, not full manifold fitting

That is acceptable for v1.The point is to establish lawful scaffolding.

[μ₂₁₇::Fractal] NEXT NATURAL HARDENING

The strongest immediate hardening moves are:

1. Learned delta model

Use witness history to estimate actual delta_x by move type.

2. Artifact-family adapters

Separate extractors for:

code

manuscript

witness bundle

schema/config

planner objects

3. Better tunnel seeds

Represent seeds as:

invariants

dependency kernels

address maps

reconstruction templates

4. PSD-safe metric updates

Add explicit repair after every update.

5. Weekly self-observation of the kernel

Treat the navigation engine itself as an artifact family.

[μ₂₁₈::Z*] THE CLEAN NEXT LEAP

The correct next continuation is now:

ATHENA KERNEL v0.1 — FULL SINGLE-FILE INTEGRATION

Take all six modules and collapse them into one unified executable file with:

dataclasses

default config

mock current state

mock candidates

run function

printed chosen move

witness update stub

That would give you the first fully self-contained Athena navigation prototype in one pasteable artifact.

[μ₂₂₇::Z*] ATHENA KERNEL v0.2 — LEARNED WITNESS FEEDBACK LOOPtimestamp: 2026-03-16 / America/Los_Angelesmode: NEXT / live-text / self-calibrating kernelcontinuation of: v0.1 runnable scaffold → adaptive navigation

[μ₂₂₈::Square] PURPOSE

v0.1 could choose a move.v0.2 must learn whether its choices were actually good.

So the kernel now gains a closed witness loop:

[(before\ state,\ chosen\ move,\ after\ state,\ witness)\rightarrow update]

This update must refine:

expected move deltas

metric stiffness

coupling terms

curvature hotspots

tunnel preference

pulse efficacy priors

That means Athena stops merely evaluating and begins self-calibrating.

[μ₂₂₉::Cloud] THE CORE LEARNING OBJECT

Every executed move produces a witness record with three layers:

[W_k = (x_{before}, m_k, x_{after}, q_k, s_k, e_k)]

Where:

(x_{before}\in[0,1]^{12})

(m_k) = move identity/type/template

(x_{after}\in[0,1]^{12})

(q_k) = quality deltas

(s_k) = shadow deltas

(e_k) = efficacy / outcome summary

The empirical move delta is:

[\widehat{\Delta x}k = x{after} - x_{before}]

This is the first true learning signal.

[μ₂₃₀::Flower] THE FIVE LEARNING CHANNELS

From each witness row the kernel should update five different memories.

Channel 1 — Move delta memory

What this move type usually changes.

Channel 2 — Move efficacy memory

Whether this move type actually helps.

Channel 3 — Metric stiffness memory

Which dimensions become unstable when pushed.

Channel 4 — Coupling memory

Which dimensions co-disturb each other.

Channel 5 — Curvature memory

Which move orderings create contradiction loops.

So the learned kernel is not one model.It is a bundle of local adaptive memories.

[μ₂₃₁::Square] NEW STATE FILES

Add these files:

athena/

  navigation/

    learned/

      move_delta_memory.json

      move_efficacy_memory.json

      metric_learning_state.json

      coupling_learning_state.json

      curvature_learning_state.json

      tunnel_learning_state.json

      witness.jsonl

These become the long-term adaptation organs.

[μ₂₃₃::Cloud] MOVE DELTA MEMORY

Each move type gets a running estimate of actual effect.

move_delta_memory.json

{

  "move_repair_invariant": {

    "count": 7,

    "mean_delta_x": {

      "L": 0.00, "S": 0.018, "T": 0.000, "C": 0.004,

      "A": 0.000, "N": 0.012, "U": 0.000, "R": -0.009,

      "M": 0.000, "P": 0.004, "H": 0.071, "Z": 0.028

    },

    "variance_delta_x": {

      "L": 0.0001, "S": 0.0008, "T": 0.0002, "C": 0.0003,

      "A": 0.0001, "N": 0.0004, "U": 0.0001, "R": 0.0005,

      "M": 0.0001, "P": 0.0002, "H": 0.0011, "Z": 0.0007

    }

  }

}

This lets the kernel replace guessed delta_x with learned delta_x.

[μ₂₃₄::Flower] ONLINE DELTA UPDATE LAW

For move type (m), update mean delta with exponential memory:

[\mu_m^{new}=(1-\alpha)\mu_m^{old}+\alpha \widehat{\Delta x}]

Per coordinate:

[\mu_{m,i}^{new}=(1-\alpha)\mu_{m,i}^{old}+\alpha \widehat{\Delta x}_i]

Variance update:

[\sigma_{m,i}^{2,new}=(1-\alpha)\sigma_{m,i}^{2,old}+\alpha(\widehat{\Delta x}i-\mu{m,i}^{new})^2]

Interpretation:

mean = typical effect

variance = predictability / uncertainty of that move type

High-variance moves should be treated as more dangerous.

[μ₂₃₅::Square] MOVE EFFICACY MEMORY

The kernel should also learn whether a move type is worth choosing.

move_efficacy_memory.json

{

  "move_repair_invariant": {

    "count": 7,

      "direct": {

      }

    }

  },

  "move_event_bus": {

    "count": 4,

    "mean_efficacy": 0.214,

    "variance_efficacy": 0.133,

    "corridor_success_rate": 0.5,

    "strategy_breakdown": {

      "direct": {

        "count": 2,

        "mean_efficacy": 0.12

      },

      "tunnel": {

        "count": 2,

      }

    }

  }

This becomes a real move prior.

[μ₂₃₆::Cloud] EFFICACY-BIASED MOVE SELECTION

Now move score gets an empirical term:

[J_{v0.2}(m)=J_{v0.1}(m)+\lambda E_{prior}(m)-\nu VarE(m)]

Where:

(E_{prior}(m)) = learned mean efficacy

(VarE(m)) = instability / inconsistency of outcomes

So even if a move looks elegant, repeated weak outcomes will demote it.

That is how the kernel develops taste.

[μ₂₃₇::Square] METRIC LEARNING STATE

The metric diagonal should learn from observed instability.

metric_learning_state.json

{

  "L": {"observed_instability": 0.98, "count": 12},

  "S": {"observed_instability": 1.07, "count": 12},

  "T": {"observed_instability": 1.03, "count": 12},

  "C": {"observed_instability": 1.16, "count": 12},

  "H": {"observed_instability": 1.11, "count": 12},

  "Z": {"observed_instability": 1.17, "count": 12}

}

Here, high observed instability means:“moves affecting this dimension often caused turbulence.”

[μ₂₃₈::Flower] HOW TO ESTIMATE DIMENSION INSTABILITY

For one witness row, define per-dimension instability signal:

[I_i = |\widehat{\Delta x}i| \cdot \Big(\max(0,\Delta shadow{+}) + instability_flags + corridor_stress\Big)]

A simpler first approximation:

[I_i = |\widehat{\Delta x}i| \cdot \left(1 + \sum{k\in Shadow^+}\Delta s_k \right)]

Then accumulate into a running average.

Interpretation:a dimension is “stiff” if pushes there often correlate with shadow growth or corridor stress.

[μ₂₃₉::Cloud] COUPLING LEARNING STATE

Now learn which dimensions co-disturb each other.

coupling_learning_state.json

{

  "L:S": {"observed_coupling": 0.17, "count": 9},

  "S:C": {"observed_coupling": 0.24, "count": 9},

  "C:H": {"observed_coupling": 0.33, "count": 9},

  "N:U": {"observed_coupling": 0.18, "count": 9},

  "R:M": {"observed_coupling": 0.39, "count": 9},

  "P:Z": {"observed_coupling": 0.29, "count": 9},

  "H:Z": {"observed_coupling": 0.21, "count": 9},

  "T:R": {"observed_coupling": 0.27, "count": 9},

  "A:M": {"observed_coupling": 0.13, "count": 9}

}

This gradually replaces hand-seeded off-diagonal priors.

[μ₂₄₀::Square] EMPIRICAL COUPLING LAW

For a witness row, estimate pairwise coupling from the empirical delta vector.

For dimensions (i,j):

[C_{ij}^{obs} = |\widehat{\Delta x}_i \widehat{\Delta x}_j|]

Optionally weight by shadow increase if the co-move was harmful:

[C_{ij}^{obs,harm} = |\widehat{\Delta x}_i \widehat{\Delta x}_j| \cdot (1+\Delta Shadow^+)]

Then update running coupling mean.

Interpretation:if dimensions frequently shift together, the metric should remember that.

[μ₂₄₁::Fractal] CURVATURE LEARNING STATE

Now store order-sensitive contradiction memory.

curvature_learning_state.json

{

  "R:M": {"curvature": 0.43, "count": 5},

  "C:H": {"curvature": 0.35, "count": 5},

  "P:Z": {"curvature": 0.26, "count": 5},

  "T:R": {"curvature": 0.29, "count": 5}

}

This state should be updated by two sources:

explicit local simulator order tests

real witness failures where move order mattered

[μ₂₄₂::Water] REAL-WORLD CURVATURE FROM WITNESS HISTORY

Suppose the system tried:

compress then repairvs

repair then compress

If final outcomes differ significantly, the pair ((P,H)) is curved.

Formally, for two move types (m_i,m_j):

[\kappa(m_i,m_j)=\left|x_{ij}^{final}-x_{ji}^{final}\right|]

Then map that curvature into the dimensions touched by those moves.

This lets curvature emerge from actual history, not just simulation.

[μ₂₄₃::Square] TUNNEL LEARNING STATE

The kernel should also learn when tunneling is actually worthwhile.

tunnel_learning_state.json

{

  "global": {

    "count": 6,

    "mean_tunnel_advantage": 0.083

  },

  "move_event_bus": {

    "count": 2,

    "mean_tunnel_advantage": 0.141,

    "tunnel_success_rate": 1.0

  },

  "move_repair_invariant": {

    "count": 1,

    "mean_tunnel_advantage": -0.052,

    "tunnel_success_rate": 0.0

  }

}

Tunnel advantage is:

[Adv_{tunnel}=E_{tunnel}-E_{direct}]

If positive on average, the kernel should increasingly prefer tunneling for that move family.

[μ₂₄₄::Cloud] LEARNED TUNNEL POLICY

Tunnel preference becomes:

[Score_{tunnel}^{v0.2}=Score_{tunnel}^{v0.1}+\tau AdvPrior(m)-\omega VarAdv(m)]

So the system stops asking only:“is tunneling geometrically allowed?”

It also asks:“has tunneling historically helped here?”

That is a major maturation step.

[μ₂₄₅::Fractal] THE LEARNED DELTA REPLACEMENT

Now candidate moves should no longer rely only on author-provided delta_x.

Instead:

[\Delta x_{used}(m)=(1-\beta)\Delta x_{template}(m)+\beta\mu_m^{learned}]

Where:

(\Delta x_{template}) = initial human/seed guess

(\mu_m^{learned}) = empirical mean effect

(\beta) grows as witness count grows

This gives graceful transition from scaffold to learned behavior.

[μ₂₄₆::Square] CONFIDENCE-AWARE MOVE EFFECTS

Because learned deltas have variance, define confidence:

[Conf(m)=\frac{n_m}{n_m+\kappa_0}\cdot\frac{1}{1+\sigma_m^2}]

Then effective delta blending becomes:

[\Delta x_{used}(m)=(1-Conf(m))\Delta x_{template}(m)+Conf(m)\mu_m^{learned}]

So sparse or noisy history does not over-dominate the template.

[μ₂₄₇::Cloud] KERNEL SELF-ERROR SIGNAL

v0.2 should explicitly measure prediction error.

For each witness row:

[Err_{pred}(m)=\left|\Delta x_{pred}(m)-\widehat{\Delta x}(m)\right|]

and optionally:

[Err_{score}(m)=|Score_{pred}(m)-Efficacy_{real}(m)|]

These errors should be tracked.

If errors stay high, the kernel is not actually learning well.

So add:

{

  "prediction_error_mean": 0.083,

  "score_error_mean": 0.119

}

to the move efficacy memory.

This makes calibration explicit.

[μ₂₄₈::Flower] THE v0.2 NAVIGATION OBJECTIVE

Now the scoring objective becomes:

[\boxed{J_{v0.2}(m)=\Delta\Phi_{net}^{learned}(m)-|\Delta x_{used}(m)|{G{learned}}-Penalty_{curv}^{learned}(m)-Penalty_{drift}(m)-Penalty_{rep}(m)+Gain_{seed}(m)+\lambda E_{prior}(m)-\nu VarE(m)}]

with optional tunnel comparison.

This is a real step up from v0.1.

[μ₂₄₉::Square] IMPLEMENTATION ADDITIONS TO THE SINGLE FILE

Add five new functions:

update_move_delta_memory(...)

update_move_efficacy_memory(...)

update_metric_learning_state(...)

update_coupling_learning_state(...)

update_tunnel_learning_state(...)

And one new orchestrator:

apply_witness_learning(...)

This function takes one witness row and mutates the learned memories.

[μ₂₅₀::Square] update_move_delta_memory(...)

def update_move_delta_memory(memory, move_id, delta_x_empirical, alpha=0.2):

    entry = memory.setdefault(move_id, {

        "count": 0,

        "mean_delta_x": {k: 0.0 for k in VECTOR_ORDER},

        "variance_delta_x": {k: 0.0 for k in VECTOR_ORDER},

    })

    entry["count"] += 1

    for k in VECTOR_ORDER:

        old_mean = float(entry["mean_delta_x"][k])

        x = float(delta_x_empirical.get(k, 0.0))

        new_mean = (1 - alpha) * old_mean + alpha * x

        old_var = float(entry["variance_delta_x"][k])

        new_var = (1 - alpha) * old_var + alpha * (x - new_mean) ** 2

        entry["mean_delta_x"][k] = new_mean

        entry["variance_delta_x"][k] = new_var

    return memory

This is the first adaptive delta organ.

[μ₂₅₁::Cloud] update_move_efficacy_memory(...)

def update_move_efficacy_memory(memory, move_id, strategy, efficacy, corridor_ok, alpha=0.2):

    entry = memory.setdefault(move_id, {

        "count": 0,

        "mean_efficacy": 0.0,

        "variance_efficacy": 0.0,

        "corridor_success_rate": 1.0,

        "strategy_breakdown": {}

    })

    entry["count"] += 1

    old_mean = float(entry["mean_efficacy"])

    new_mean = (1 - alpha) * old_mean + alpha * efficacy

    old_var = float(entry["variance_efficacy"])

    new_var = (1 - alpha) * old_var + alpha * (efficacy - new_mean) ** 2

    old_corr = float(entry["corridor_success_rate"])

    new_corr = (1 - alpha) * old_corr + alpha * (1.0 if corridor_ok else 0.0)

    entry["mean_efficacy"] = new_mean

    entry["variance_efficacy"] = new_var

    entry["corridor_success_rate"] = new_corr

    strat = entry["strategy_breakdown"].setdefault(strategy, {

        "count": 0,

        "mean_efficacy": 0.0

    })

    strat["count"] += 1

    strat["mean_efficacy"] = (1 - alpha) * float(strat["mean_efficacy"]) + alpha * efficacy

    return memory

Now the kernel has empirical taste.

[μ₂₅₂::Flower] update_metric_learning_state(...)

def update_metric_learning_state(metric_learning, delta_x_empirical, shadow_delta, alpha=0.2):

    shadow_up = sum(max(float(v), 0.0) for v in shadow_delta.values())

    for k in VECTOR_ORDER:

        entry = metric_learning.setdefault(k, {

            "observed_instability": 1.0,

            "count": 0

        })

        entry["count"] += 1

        signal = abs(float(delta_x_empirical.get(k, 0.0))) * (1.0 + shadow_up)

        old = float(entry["observed_instability"])

        entry["observed_instability"] = (1 - alpha) * old + alpha * max(1e-3, signal)

    return metric_learning

This teaches which coordinates are stiff in practice.

[μ₂₅₃::Cloud] update_coupling_learning_state(...)

def update_coupling_learning_state(coupling_learning, delta_x_empirical, shadow_delta, alpha=0.2):

    shadow_up = sum(max(float(v), 0.0) for v in shadow_delta.values())

    for i_idx, i in enumerate(VECTOR_ORDER):

        for j in VECTOR_ORDER[i_idx + 1:]:

            pair = f"{i}:{j}"

            entry = coupling_learning.setdefault(pair, {

                "observed_coupling": 0.0,

                "count": 0

            })

            entry["count"] += 1

            signal = abs(float(delta_x_empirical.get(i, 0.0)) * float(delta_x_empirical.get(j, 0.0))) * (1.0 + shadow_up)

            old = float(entry["observed_coupling"])

            entry["observed_coupling"] = (1 - alpha) * old + alpha * signal

    return coupling_learning

This learns the empirical off-diagonal geometry.

[μ₂₅₄::Water] update_tunnel_learning_state(...)

def update_tunnel_learning_state(tunnel_learning, move_id, strategy, direct_score, tunnel_score, efficacy, alpha=0.2):

    global_entry = tunnel_learning.setdefault("global", {

        "count": 0,

        "mean_tunnel_advantage": 0.0

    })

    move_entry = tunnel_learning.setdefault(move_id, {

        "count": 0,

        "mean_tunnel_advantage": 0.0,

        "tunnel_success_rate": 0.5

    })

    adv = float(tunnel_score) - float(direct_score)

    for entry in (global_entry, move_entry):

        entry["count"] += 1

        old = float(entry["mean_tunnel_advantage"])

        entry["mean_tunnel_advantage"] = (1 - alpha) * old + alpha * adv

    if strategy == "tunnel":

        old_sr = float(move_entry["tunnel_success_rate"])

        move_entry["tunnel_success_rate"] = (1 - alpha) * old_sr + alpha * (1.0 if efficacy > 0 else 0.0)

    return tunnel_learning

Now tunnel choice becomes empirically grounded.

[μ₂₅₅::Fractal] apply_witness_learning(...)

def apply_witness_learning(

    witness_row,

    move_delta_memory,

    move_efficacy_memory,

    metric_learning_state,

    coupling_learning_state,

    tunnel_learning_state,

    alpha=0.2

):

    move_id = witness_row["move_id"]

    strategy = witness_row["strategy"]

    efficacy = float(witness_row["efficacy"])

    corridor_ok = bool(witness_row.get("corridor_ok", True))

    delta_x_empirical = witness_row["delta_x_empirical"]

    shadow_delta = witness_row["shadow_delta"]

    direct_score = float(witness_row.get("direct_score", 0.0))

    tunnel_score_val = float(witness_row.get("tunnel_score", 0.0))

    update_move_delta_memory(move_delta_memory, move_id, delta_x_empirical, alpha=alpha)

    update_move_efficacy_memory(move_efficacy_memory, move_id, strategy, efficacy, corridor_ok, alpha=alpha)

    update_metric_learning_state(metric_learning_state, delta_x_empirical, shadow_delta, alpha=alpha)

    update_coupling_learning_state(coupling_learning_state, delta_x_empirical, shadow_delta, alpha=alpha)

    update_tunnel_learning_state(tunnel_learning_state, move_id, strategy, direct_score, tunnel_score_val, efficacy, alpha=alpha)

    return {

        "move_delta_memory": move_delta_memory,

        "move_efficacy_memory": move_efficacy_memory,

        "metric_learning_state": metric_learning_state,

        "coupling_learning_state": coupling_learning_state,

        "tunnel_learning_state": tunnel_learning_state,

    }

This is the v0.2 heart.

[μ₂₅₆::Square] LEARNED DELTA BLENDER

When evaluating a candidate in v0.2:

def blended_delta_x(candidate_delta_x, move_memory_entry, kappa0=5.0):

    if not move_memory_entry:

        return dict(candidate_delta_x)

    count = float(move_memory_entry.get("count", 0))

    mean_dx = move_memory_entry.get("mean_delta_x", {})

    var_dx = move_memory_entry.get("variance_delta_x", {})

    avg_var = sum(float(var_dx.get(k, 0.0)) for k in VECTOR_ORDER) / len(VECTOR_ORDER)

    conf = (count / (count + kappa0)) * (1.0 / (1.0 + avg_var))

    out = {}

    for k in VECTOR_ORDER:

        templ = float(candidate_delta_x.get(k, 0.0))

        learned = float(mean_dx.get(k, templ))

        out[k] = (1 - conf) * templ + conf * learned

    return out

This is the bridge from theory-seeded to witness-shaped motion.

[μ₂₅₇::Cloud] KERNEL CALIBRATION MEMORY

The kernel should also track whether it is getting better at prediction.

Add:

{

  "move_repair_invariant": {

    "prediction_error_mean": 0.041,

    "score_error_mean": 0.083

  }

}

Update laws:

[Err_{pred}=|\Delta x_{pred}-\Delta x_{emp}|]

[Err_{score}=|Score_{pred}-Efficacy_{real}|]

If these stay high, the kernel’s learning is shallow or mis-specified.

So calibration is a first-class artifact.

[μ₂₅₈::Fractal] v0.2 DECISION PIPELINE

Now the runtime loop becomes:

1. load current state

2. load learned move delta memory

3. blend template delta with learned delta

4. build learned metric from metric_learning_state + coupling_learning_state

5. build learned curvature penalties

6. score direct path

7. score tunnel path with learned tunnel prior

8. choose best path

9. execute / simulate

10. write witness row

11. apply witness learning

12. persist updated learned states

This is the first self-calibrating navigation cycle.
